    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9858900155617993646">I am Funny Like That is a collection of stories about my life and fictional short stories. I enjoy making people laugh out loud, think about things differently or get engaged in a conversation about life. No matter who you are the one thing we all have in common is we like to laugh. It makes us feel better, it makes us like people and it cures the soul. <br/>This book was writt</span>
  <span id="freeText9858900155617993646" style="display:none">I am Funny Like That is a collection of stories about my life and fictional short stories. I enjoy making people laugh out loud, think about things differently or get engaged in a conversation about life. No matter who you are the one thing we all have in common is we like to laugh. It makes us feel better, it makes us like people and it cures the soul. <br />This book was written to get the craziness out of my head and on to paper. It was also written for the mothers, fathers, caregivers, and people in general who are going through life wondering “Am I the only one who thinks this way?” Well no you are not. Lots of us think that way and laughing about it is how we cope. <br />So grab a cup of tea or a glass of wine, light a candle and curl up with I am Funny Like That and start laughing.</span>

    <a title="Paragraph And A Half" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73320982-paragraph-and-a-half"><img alt="Paragraph And A Half" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1526474966p2/73320982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2171717408?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paragraph And A Half" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paragraph And A Half" href="/user/show/73320982-paragraph-and-a-half">Paragraph And A Half</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2171717408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14980902569491549881">I’ve read a lot of serious books recently and I Am Funny Like That was just what I needed right now. Some light-hearted fun, and I know books claim to be able to make you laugh out loud, but this one really did. Behind a lot of the humour is an underlying commentary at modern life and society that is as insightful as it is funny. <br/><br/>After learning that Escott’s book was based on her blog posts I went to look at that and can see there’s a lot more material for future books. So now I’m a fan and eage</span>
  <span id="freeText14980902569491549881" style="display:none">I’ve read a lot of serious books recently and I Am Funny Like That was just what I needed right now. Some light-hearted fun, and I know books claim to be able to make you laugh out loud, but this one really did. Behind a lot of the humour is an underlying commentary at modern life and society that is as insightful as it is funny. <br /><br />After learning that Escott’s book was based on her blog posts I went to look at that and can see there’s a lot more material for future books. So now I’m a fan and eager to see what comes next. <br /><br />The kind of book you immediately love and want to give copies to friends so you can discuss it with them.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14980902569491549881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1749295403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1749295403" />
    <a title="Helen Escott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58565467-helen-escott"><img alt="Helen Escott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531760065p2/58565467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1749295403?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen Escott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen Escott" href="/user/show/58565467-helen-escott">Helen Escott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span> (Review from the author)
          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781483578170" href="/book/show/31819605-i-am-funny-like-that">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1749295403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3103237278595150879">Reviewed By Viga Boland for Readers’ Favorite<br/><br/>There is no doubt about it: Helen C. Escott, author of I Am Funny Like That, is a very funny lady who loves to laugh, and loves to make others laugh with her. Just look at that book cover! So clever and it sets the mood of I am Funny Like That before you even open the book. Helen C. Scott just happens to be very good at making people, especially women, laugh. Her blog by the same name has had over 100,000 visitors. Obviously, she’s certainly struck a </span>
  <span id="freeText3103237278595150879" style="display:none">Reviewed By Viga Boland for Readers’ Favorite<br /><br />There is no doubt about it: Helen C. Escott, author of I Am Funny Like That, is a very funny lady who loves to laugh, and loves to make others laugh with her. Just look at that book cover! So clever and it sets the mood of I am Funny Like That before you even open the book. Helen C. Scott just happens to be very good at making people, especially women, laugh. Her blog by the same name has had over 100,000 visitors. Obviously, she’s certainly struck a chord with all who need a good laugh…and who doesn’t? So it’s only good sense to do as Helen C. Escott has now done and that is to compile those hilarious blog posts into a book. Producing a book from your blog posts is today becoming a popular practice. Now some might think why buy the book when you can just go online and read the blog? That's true. But not everyone has time for or likes reading computer screens. So a book makes good sense.<br /><br />In I Am Funny Like That, Helen C. Scott chatters on happily about all the things most of us, especially women, live with, enjoy, and groan about from day to day. You find yourself instantly relating to her. In almost every post, I recognized myself. She agonizes over her menopausal belly which refuses to fit neatly into her spandex underwear. So do I. She curses those miserable chin hairs that belong on her husband’s chin and not hers. Ditto! And while I didn’t read 50 Shades of Grey as Helen did, like her I wondered if I could also become famous by writing a version of that book for women my age. When she decides she needs some sexy new lingerie (wonder if 50 Shades had anything to do with that?) she discovers to her surprise, that today’s modern girls wear bras with metal tassels. Not really her kind of thing, nor mine! <br /><br />Helen also has a habit, as most of us do, of completing her husband’s sentences in her head with her own thoughts, and then wondering how she misunderstood what he was trying to say. Me too. You too? And like so many of us who have children, she also gets annoyed with everyone telling her how to raise a child, especially when the advice comes from those who’ve never had one. Boy, have I met a lot of those! Along with recognizing myself in so much of what Helen C. Escott chatters on about in I Am Funny Like That, I particularly enjoyed her clever one liners e.g. “Can you imagine if Elvis sent out a tweet every time he moved? The whole internet would be all shook up.” <br /><br />She could be a stand-up comedian as she pops this type of stuff out. It’s obvious she loves playing on and with words, She has a very sharp wit you can’t help but admire. At the same time, when she muses on the fact that modern teens would rather be famous than intelligent, while women in so many cultures would just love the opportunity to get an education, you know that behind the laughter is a caring, deep, and thoughtful woman. <br /><br />I am Funny Like That by Helen C Scott is the kind book I dreamed of writing, the kind Erma Bombeck was famous for: a book that hits home with homemakers on so many levels. I forgive Helen for publishing a book I wanted to write because she's done such a great job. I really enjoyed reading I am Funny Like That, because I believe we can never have too much laughter, only too little. So thanks, Helen, for giving me more reasons to smile in my sometimes not so funny life.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3103237278595150879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2051234020" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2051234020?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Texjim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Texjim" href="/user/show/48103555-texjim">Texjim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2051234020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14413300944487039320">First, for a book which uses the word funny twice on the front cover, I found this read amusing at best. This is a selection of columns from the Author's blog a retired communications specialist with the RCMP. It is all not intended to be humor and does get somewhat preachy at times. Overall It's target audience is clearly not me (a retired old man), but more likely the average middle aged woman who has struggled with raising a family and growing older. There are a lot of anecdotes which I am su</span>
  <span id="freeText14413300944487039320" style="display:none">First, for a book which uses the word funny twice on the front cover, I found this read amusing at best. This is a selection of columns from the Author's blog a retired communications specialist with the RCMP. It is all not intended to be humor and does get somewhat preachy at times. Overall It's target audience is clearly not me (a retired old man), but more likely the average middle aged woman who has struggled with raising a family and growing older. There are a lot of anecdotes which I am sure simply make most of that target audience smile and nod in agreement. I doubt anyone would be laughing out loud as this is a discussion of the humor in life's everyday events. The writing is fairly clear and there are no concerns about subject matter or language which are both PG. If you expecting Erma Bombeck, you may be disappointed. However, if you are part of the target demographic, you may enjoy this as an amusing look at everyday life. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14413300944487039320" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VKGoAhfHni2auDTh0okxslU60hkmnn7LK9QSCNSTrRyunAOm8HU49adsoTxw5gWotKRbk4sr9zHIZP71UAEitg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

Sometimes rural idyll, sometimes hell on earth, Paul’s life in rural Kent has been shared over the years with some very vocal pigs, a mad cow, various rescued barn owls, the world’s most sadistic geese and Christine the psychotic sheep – among many other animal waifs and strays. And of course Paul tells the stories of the dogs in his life – including the tiny chihuahua/Jack Russell cross with Napoleonic ambitions, Eddie, Miss Olga, Bullseye, Louis, Boycie and, of course, Buster, the greatest canine star since Lassie. In addition, Paul shares some of his favourite recipes, explores country lore and superstitions, and extols the benefits of growing your own vegetables, herbs and fruit.This is a warts-and-all account of country living, as far removed from the bright lights of celebrity as you could ever imagine. The trials and tribulations Paul experienced on moving to deepest darkest Kent as a dyed-in-the-wool city dweller are every bit as hilarious and eventful as you would think. He had a lot of new skills to learn, and fast: everything from how to churn your own butter and how to birth a lamb to the best way to lure a cow out of your kitchen while naked from the waist down.Brilliantly funny and full of classic stories, Paul O’Grady’s Country Life is your armchair guide to the wonders and horrors of rural existence.<\/span>\n  <a Built in 1903 on the dusty outskirts of Arlington, a remote dot between Dallas and Fort Worth\'s red-light districts, the progressive home bucks public opinion by offering faith, training, and rehabilitation to prostitutes, addicts, unwed mothers, and &quot;ruined&quot; girls without forcibly separating mothers from children. When Lizzie Bates and Mattie McBride meet there--one sick and abused, but desperately clinging to her young daughter, the other jilted by the beau who fathered her ailing son--they form a friendship that will see them through unbearable loss, heartbreak, difficult choices, and ultimately, diverging paths.\n\nA century later, Cate Sutton, a reclusive university librarian, uncovers the hidden histories of the two troubled women as she stumbles upon the cemetery on the home\'s former grounds and begins to comb through its archives in her library. Pulled by an indescribable connection, what Cate discovers about their stories leads her to confront her own heartbreaking past, and to reclaim the life she thought she\'d let go forever. In this groundbreaking work, therapist Resmaa Menakem examines the damage caused by racism in America from the perspective of body-centered psychology. He argues this destruction will continue until Americans learn to heal the generational anguish of white supremacy, which is deeply embedded in all our bodies. Our collective agony doesn\'t just affect African Americans. White Americans suffer their own secondary trauma as well. So do blue Americans—our police.\n\nMy Grandmother\'s Hands is a call to action for all of us to recognize that racism is not about the head, but about the body, and introduces an alternative view of what we can do to grow beyond our entrenched racialized divide.\n\n\n\nPaves the way for a new, body-centered understanding of white supremacy—how it is literally in our blood and our nervous system.\n\n\nOffers a step-by-step solution—a healing process—in addition to incisive social commentary.\n\nResmaa Menakem, MSW, LICSW, is a therapist with decades of experience currently in private practice in Minneapolis, MN, specializing in trauma, body-centered psychotherapy, and violence prevention. He has appeared on the Oprah Winfrey Show and Dr. Phil as an expert on conflict and violence. Menakem has studied with bestselling authors Dr. David Schnarch (Passionate Marriage) and Dr. Bessel van der Kolk (The Body Keeps the Score).
